        if (hasPeriod || hasUppercase) {
          newPath = newPath.replace(/\./g, '-').toLowerCase();
          if (!newPath.endsWith('/')) {
            newPath += '/';

Use Xano as Bubble’s external backend for data, auth, and workflows.","setup_instructions":"At Xano, we understand that building a powerful backend for your web or mobile application can be a daunting task, especially if you're not a seasoned developer. That's why we've created a seamless integration with Bubble, a leading no code app builder for creating web applications. By connecting your Xano API endpoints to Bubble, you can leverage the power of Xano's backend services and use Bubble for the frontend, to develop web applications faster and more effectively.\n\nIn this step-by-step guide, we'll show you how to connect your Xano API endpoints to Bubble, allowing you to use Xano as your backend and Bubble as your frontend. Let's get started!\n\n## Step 1: Install the Bubble API Connector\n\nThe first step is to ensure that you have the Bubble API Connector installed. This plugin allows Bubble to communicate with external APIs, including your Xano API endpoints.\n\n1. In Bubble, navigate to the \"Plugins\" page.\n\n2. Search for the \"Bubble API Connector\" and install it.\n\n## Step 2: Connect a GET Endpoint\n\nNow that you have the API Connector installed, it's time to connect your first Xano API endpoint to Bubble. Let's start with a GET endpoint.\n\n1. In Xano, locate the GET endpoint you want to connect. For example, the \"GET all merchant records\" endpoint.\n\n2. Copy the endpoint URL by clicking the link icon.\n\n3. In Bubble, go back to the \"Plugins\" page and expand the Bubble API Connector.\n\n4. Click \"Add API\" and give your API a descriptive name, such as \"GET Merchants.\"\n\n5. Paste the copied endpoint URL into the \"API URL\" field.\n\n6. Click \"Initialize Call.\"\n\n7. Bubble will automatically detect and display the fields from your Xano database table.\n\n8. Review the field types and make any necessary adjustments.\n\n9. Click \"Save\" to finalize the connection.\n\nCongratulations! You've successfully connected your first Xano GET endpoint to Bubble.\n\n## Step 3: Connect a POST Endpoint\n\nConnecting a POST endpoint to Bubble requires an additional step due to the need for request body parameters.\n\n1. In Xano, locate the POST endpoint you want to connect. For example, the \"POST merchant record\" endpoint.\n\n2. Copy the endpoint URL by clicking the link icon.\n\n3. In Bubble, go back to the \"Plugins\" page and expand the Bubble API Connector.\n\n4. Click \"Add API\" and give your API a descriptive name, such as \"POST Merchant.\"\n\n5. Paste the copied endpoint URL into the \"API URL\" field.\n\n6. Change the HTTP method from \"GET\" to \"POST\" using the dropdown menu.\n\n7. In Xano, navigate to the Swagger documentation for the same endpoint.\n\n8. Copy the example request body provided in the Swagger documentation.\n\n9. In Bubble, paste the copied request body into the \"Request Body\" field.\n\n10. Replace any dynamic values with Bubble's dynamic value syntax (e.g., {{myVariable}}).\n\n11. Click \"Initialize Call.\"\n\n12. Bubble will automatically detect and display the fields from your Xano database table.\n\n13. Review the field types and make any necessary adjustments.\n\n14. Click \"Save\" to finalize the connection.\n\nWell done! By leveraging Xano's backend-as-a-service capabilities and Drapcode's intuitive front-end development tools, developers can create scalable, maintainable applications with ease.\n\nThis comprehensive guide outlines the steps to seamlessly integrate Xano and Drapcode.\n\n## Overview of Xano and Drapcode\n\n**Xano** is a versatile backend-as-a-service platform designed to simplify database management, API creation, and server-side logic through a no-code environment. It offers robust features for building and managing backend infrastructure, making it an ideal choice for developers seeking efficient backend solutions.\n\n**Drapcode**, on the other hand, is a feature-rich front-end development tool that empowers developers to create web applications using intuitive drag-and-drop functionalities. With Drapcode, developers can design responsive and visually appealing interfaces without writing extensive code, significantly accelerating the development process.\n\n## Steps to Integrate Xano and Drapcode\n\n### 1. Setting Up Xano and Drapcode\n\nBegin by creating a new project in both **Xano** and **Drapcode**.\n\n#### Xano Setup:\n\n- Set up **tables** in Xano with appropriate fields to define your data structure.\n\n- Configure **API endpoints** in Xano to access and manipulate data stored in the tables.\n\n#### Drapcode Setup:\n\n- Create a new **Drapcode project** to initiate the front-end development process.\n\n- Familiarize yourself with Drapcode's interface and available components.\n\n---\n\n### 2. Establishing Connection Between Xano and Drapcode\n\nTo establish a connection between Xano and Drapcode, you’ll need to set up **external API integrations** in Drapcode.\n\n#### Create External API Endpoints:\n\n1. In Drapcode, navigate to **Settings → External API** to create new external API endpoints.\n\n2. This plugin allows Bubble to communicate with external APIs, including your Xano API endpoints.\n\n1. In Bubble, navigate to the \"Plugins\" page.\n\n2. Search for the \"Bubble API Connector\" and install it.\n\n## Step 2: Connect a GET Endpoint\n\nNow that you have the API Connector installed, it's time to connect your first Xano API endpoint to Bubble. Let's start with a GET endpoint.\n\n1. In Xano, locate the GET endpoint you want to connect. For example, the \"GET all merchant records\" endpoint.\n\n2. Copy the endpoint URL by clicking the link icon.\n\n3. In Bubble, go back to the \"Plugins\" page and expand the Bubble API Connector.\n\n4. Click \"Add API\" and give your API a descriptive name, such as \"GET Merchants.\"\n\n5. Paste the copied endpoint URL into the \"API URL\" field.\n\n6. Click \"Initialize Call.\"\n\n7. Bubble will automatically detect and display the fields from your Xano database table.\n\n8. Review the field types and make any necessary adjustments.\n\n9. Click \"Save\" to finalize the connection.\n\nCongratulations! You've successfully connected your first Xano GET endpoint to Bubble.\n\n## Step 3: Connect a POST Endpoint\n\nConnecting a POST endpoint to Bubble requires an additional step due to the need for request body parameters.\n\n1. In Xano, locate the POST endpoint you want to connect. For example, the \"POST merchant record\" endpoint.\n\n2. Copy the endpoint URL by clicking the link icon.\n\n3. In Bubble, go back to the \"Plugins\" page and expand the Bubble API Connector.\n\n4. Click \"Add API\" and give your API a descriptive name, such as \"POST Merchant.\"\n\n5. Paste the copied endpoint URL into the \"API URL\" field.\n\n6. Change the HTTP method from \"GET\" to \"POST\" using the dropdown menu.\n\n7. In Xano, navigate to the Swagger documentation for the same endpoint.\n\n8. Copy the example request body provided in the Swagger documentation.\n\n9. In Bubble, paste the copied request body into the \"Request Body\" field.\n\n10. Replace any dynamic values with Bubble's dynamic value syntax (e.g., {{myVariable}}).\n\n11. Click \"Initialize Call.\"\n\n12. Bubble will automatically detect and display the fields from your Xano database table.\n\n13. Review the field types and make any necessary adjustments.\n\n14. Click \"Save\" to finalize the connection.\n\nWell done! You've successfully connected both a GET and a POST endpoint from Xano to Bubble, enabling you to leverage Xano's powerful backend services while building your application's frontend with Bubble's no-code tools.\n\nBy following these steps, you've unlocked the potential to create robust and scalable applications without writing a single line of code. Add a new data source and choose **Xano** from the list.\n   - Paste the copied access token into the **Access Token** input field.\n   - Select the Xano workspace you want to connect from the dropdown menu.\n\n## Automatic Schema Analysis\n\nOnce connected, **Noloco** will analyze the data in your **Xano** database and automatically create tables and views in your app based on your data from Xano.\n\nFor example, if you have a table with *Properties* data in Xano, Noloco will create:\n\n- A **collection list view**\n\n- A **record view** to edit individual records\n\n- A **form** to add new *Properties* data\n\n## Supported Field Types\n\n**Noloco** supports various field types from **Xano**, including:\n\n- Integer\n\n- Decimal\n\n- Timestamp (Date and Time)\n\n- Email\n\n- Text (single line)\n\n- Enum\n\n- Boolean\n\n- Image\n\n- File / Attachment\n\n- Video\n\n- Audio\n\n- Object\n\n- Geo Point\n\n- Reference to table\n\nFor a complete list of supported field types, refer to the documentation.\n\n## Frequently Asked Questions\n\n**How often does my data get synced?**\n\n- Data updates from Noloco are reflected instantly in your Xano database.\n\n- Direct updates to your Xano base are synced to Noloco in less than 2 minutes.\n\n**Can I connect multiple Xano workspaces to my Noloco app?**\n\n- Yes, you can connect multiple Xano workspaces to the same Noloco app.\n\n**Why isn't my Xano base appearing in the dropdown to connect?**\n\n- Ensure that Noloco has access to your workspace from your Personal Access Token.\n\n**Why won't one of my fields sync?**\n\n- Some field types may not be supported by Noloco. Refer to the documentation for details.\n\n- Field name clashes with existing columns may prevent synchronization.\n\n**What about custom functions on the Xano API?**\n\n- Noloco doesn't use custom Xano API functions, but alternative solutions can be explored based on your needs.\n\n## Conclusion\n\nBy connecting **Xano** with **Noloco**, you can leverage the power of no-code development to build sophisticated applications effortlessly. With Drapcode, developers can design responsive and visually appealing interfaces without writing extensive code, significantly accelerating the development process.\n\n## Steps to Integrate Xano and Drapcode\n\n### 1. Setting Up Xano and Drapcode\n\nBegin by creating a new project in both **Xano** and **Drapcode**.\n\n#### Xano Setup:\n\n- Set up **tables** in Xano with appropriate fields to define your data structure.\n\n- Configure **API endpoints** in Xano to access and manipulate data stored in the tables.\n\n#### Drapcode Setup:\n\n- Create a new **Drapcode project** to initiate the front-end development process.\n\n- Familiarize yourself with Drapcode's interface and available components.\n\n---\n\n### 2. Establishing Connection Between Xano and Drapcode\n\nTo establish a connection between Xano and Drapcode, you’ll need to set up **external API integrations** in Drapcode.\n\n#### Create External API Endpoints:\n\n1. In Drapcode, navigate to **Settings → External API** to create new external API endpoints.\n\n2. Define endpoints for **fetching**, **creating**, **updating**, and **deleting** data in Xano.\n\n---\n\n### 3. Fetching and Displaying Data in Drapcode\n\nUse Drapcode’s components to fetch data from Xano and display it in your web application.\n\n#### Data Retrieval:\n\n- Configure Drapcode to make **API requests** to fetch data from Xano endpoints.\n\n- Map the retrieved data to Drapcode components for display, such as tables, cards, or text blocks.\n\n---\n\n### 4. Interacting with Data: Create, Update, Delete Operations\n\nEnable **CRUD (Create, Read, Update, Delete)** operations in your Drapcode application to interact with data stored in Xano.\n\n#### Creating Records:\n\n- Set up **forms** in Drapcode to create new records.\n\n- Configure form submissions to trigger **API requests** to Xano for data creation.\n\n#### Updating Records:\n\n- Implement functionality in Drapcode to allow users to **update existing records**.\n\n- Configure Drapcode to send **update requests** to Xano endpoints.\n\n#### Deleting Records:\n\n- Enable deletion of records directly from your Drapcode application.\n\n- Implement functionality to send **delete requests** to Xano endpoints.\n\n---\n\n## Conclusion\n\nIntegrating **Xano** with **Drapcode** offers developers a streamlined workflow for building dynamic web applications.\n\nBy following the steps outlined in this guide, developers can harness the combined power of **Xano’s backend capabilities** and **Drapcode’s front-end tools** to create robust, scalable, and visually appealing applications efficiently.\n\nWhether you're developing a simple website or a complex web application, integrating **Xano** and **Drapcode** provides a flexible and intuitive solution for your development needs.","vendor_category_id":9,"featured":false,"active":true,"image_link":null,"skipEmpty":true,"integrations":[{"id":120,"Description":"Fetch and Display Data in a Table","Type":"Tutorial","Vendor_ID":45,"Link":"https://youtu.be/jVOd_5FwLD4","vendors_id":45,"xano_description":"Integrate DrapCode functionality into your Xano workflows using this tutorial.
